Patient: STEPHENSON, CORY MRN: T002016069 FIN: T[PHONE-536]
Age: 27 Years Sex: Male DOB: [DOB-1]
Chief Complaint
R9 - MVA RESTRAINED DRIVER +LOC -THINNERS
History of Present Illness
27-year-old male with no reported past medical history presents after MVA just prior to
arrival. Patient was the restrained driver of a vehicle involved in an accident at high
speeds. Positive LOC. Not on anticoagulants. Patient is reporting pain to his mid/lower
back as well as his left knee. He has no other focal areas of pain. Denies chest pain,
dyspnea, abdominal pain, numbness, tingling, weakness, or any other symptoms at this
time.
Physical Exam
General: alert, no acute distress
Skin: warm, dry
HENT: normocephalic, atraumatic
Eye: PERRL, EOMI, normal conjunctiva
Neck: no midline tenderness or deformity
Cardiovascular: RRR, no murmur, normal peripheral perfusion, no edema
Chest Wall: no tenderness, no deformity
Respiratory: lungs CTA, non-labored respirations, BS equal bilaterally
Gastrointestinal: soft, nontender, nondistended
Back: midline T/L spine tenderness, normal alignment, no step-offs
Musculoskeletal: L knee tenderness with small superficial abrasion, PMS intact; no
other bony tenderness/deformity
Neurological: A&Ox4, no focal neuro deficits
Medical Decision Making
Room 9 Course:
EMS Notification Prior to Arrival: yes
Vitals Upon Arrival: per nurses notes
Medications
No qualifying data available
No qualifying data available

Primary Survey: 
 - Airway:intact, speaking
 - Breathing:spontaneous respirations, equal BS
 - Circulation: good peripheral circulation with heart sounds appreciable
 - Disability: GCS15/15, moving all extremities spontaneously, PERRL
Placed on monitor, peripheral IVs obtained.
Secondary Survey: see above
Imaging Obtained in Room 9:
 - CXR : CXR with no obvious pneumo/hemothorax, pleural effusion, or focal
consolidation.
Treatments Provided: fentanyl 100 mcg IV
Procedures Performed in Room 9: none
Consults in Room 9: none
Vitals on Room 9 Exit: see nursing notes
Attending: Dr. O'Brien was present and available throughout
Initial Differential: neurologic injury, spinal injury, intrathoracic injury, intraabdominal
injury, vascular injury, fracture, dislocation
Disposition: to CT
ED Clinical Course:
Patient was initially evaluated in room 9. Exam was significant for midline T/L-spine
tenderness, neurologically intact. Hemodynamically stable. Taken from room 9 to CT
for Man scan, which ultimately showed no acute traumatic injuries. CT lumbar spine
showed a 8 x 6 mm sclerotic focus in the posterior body of T3, which could potentially
represent a bone island. Patient was notified of this finding and recommended to
follow-up with PCP for further evaluation and monitoring. Lab workup was reassuring. 
Patient was provided with multimodal pain control while in the ED. Able to ambulate
without assistance and tolerate p.o. without difficulty. Discussed reassuring workup and
plan for discharge home. Provided with prescriptions for Tylenol, ibuprofen, lidocaine
patch, and Robaxin as needed for pain. Return precautions provided, including
numbness, tingling, weakness, or any other new/concerning symptoms. Patient
understood and agreeable with plan.
Imaging Reviewed: CT Head with no obvious intracranial hemorrhage. CT Chest with
no obvious pneumo/hemothorax, pulmonary contusions, or tamponade. CT Abd/Pelvis
with no obvious large volume free fluid. CT C/T/L-Spine with no obvious spinal
malalignment or canal impingement.
- I personally interpreted/reviewed all scans/imaging ordered today as they resulted in
real time. In addition, I reviewed the final Radiologist’s interpretations as well.
Disposition: Discharge home

Authorized and Performed by: Matthew Lyons, DO
Total critical care time: Approximately 31 minutes
Due to a high probability of clinically significant, life threatening deterioration, the patient
required my highest level of preparedness to intervene emergently and I personally
spent this critical care time directly and personally managing the patient. This critical
care time included obtaining a history; examining the patient; pulse oximetry; ordering
and review of studies; arranging urgent treatment with development of a management
plan; evaluation of patient’s response to treatment; frequent reassessment; and,
discussions with other providers. 
This critical care time was performed to assess and manage the high probability of
imminent, life-threatening deterioration that could result in multi-organ failure. It was
exclusive of separately billable procedures and treating other patients and teaching
time. 
Please see MDM section and the rest of the note for further information on patient
assessment and treatment

1. Motor vehicle accident
2. Back pain

You Need to Schedule the Following Appointments
Follow Up with Home Pain Control -
Tylenol & Ibuprofen
Why: Home Pain Control: Tylenol & Ibuprofen
Acetaminophen (Tylenol): 1000 mg every 8 hours as needed for pain
- You should be aware that other medications may include acetaminophen. Please ensure that if you are
taking any other medications that contain acetaminophen, that you do not exceed a total of 4000 mg from
all sources in 24 hours.
Ibuprofen: 600 mg every 6-8 hours as needed for pain
If you are continuing to require both of these medications every 6-8 hours for more than 3-5 consecutive
days, you should follow up with your primary care physician for repeat evaluation. If you feel that you need
to be seen more urgently or have worsening of your symptoms, please return to the emergency
department.
Follow Up with General Discharge
Instructions
Why: General Discharge Instructions
- You have received an emergency department evaluation. This evaluation is intended to rule out
life-threatening conditions, it is not a complete evaluation. You could require further diagnostic testing as
determined by your primary care provider or any referred specialist.
- Please follow up with your primary care provider within 48-72 hours. Call for an appointment as soon as
possible.
- Please continue taking your home medications and take any new medications as prescribed.
- Please follow all discharge instructions.
Reasons to Return to the Emergency Department
- Please return to the Emergency Department if you develop worsening pain, inability to tolerate eating or
drinking, chest pain, shortness of breath, difficulty moving or feeling any part of your body, or you have any
other symptoms which concern you.

regarding your home medications to your Primary Care Provider.
Take your medications faithfully. Do NOT skip medication. Do NOT stop taking medications without the direction of a health care
provider. Carry a list of your medications with you at all times, and take this medication list with you to your first follow up visit. Report
any side effects. Avoid herbal remedies unless discussed with your provider.
As part of your treatment plan, your provider may have prescribed a limited course of a controlled substance. This medication may be
given to help people with moderate or severe pain or for other medical conditions, but there are risks involved with treatment. Common
side effects may include nausea, constipation, drowsiness, sweating, itching, dry mouth, and rash. More serious side effects may
include cognitive and motor impairment, like problems with thinking, concentrating, alertness, and movement (e.g. slowed reflexes), and

Education Materials
Acute Back Pain, Adult
Acute back pain is sudden and usually short-lived. It is often caused by an injury to the muscles and tissues in the back. The injury may
result from:
• A muscle, tendon, or ligament getting overstretched or torn. Ligaments are tissues that connect bones to each other. Lifting
something improperly can cause a back strain.
• Wear and tear (degeneration) of the spinal disks. Spinal disks are circular tissue that provide cushioning between the bones of
the spine (vertebrae).
• Twisting motions, such as while playing sports or doing yard work.
• A hit to the back.
• Arthritis.
You may have a physical exam, lab tests, and imaging tests to find the cause of your pain. Acute back pain usually goes away with rest
and home care.
Follow these instructions at home:

which means that the body has gotten used to them and may experience withdrawal symptoms, if they are abruptly stopped. Withdrawal
symptoms can include runny nose, sweating, goose bumps, diarrhea, abdominal cramping, rapid heartbeat, difficulty sleeping, and
nervousness. Please dispose of unused and expired medications per pharmacy guidance.

Emergency
Managing pain, stiffness, and swelling
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider. Treatment may include medicines
for pain and inflammation that are taken by mouth or applied to the skin, or muscle relaxants.
• Your health care provider may recommend applying ice during the first 24–48 hours after your pain starts. To do this:
—46 Put ice in a plastic bag.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
—46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day.
—46 Remove the ice if your skin turns bright red. This is very important. If you cannot feel pain, heat, or cold, you have a
greater risk of damage to the area.
• If directed, apply heat to the affected area as often as told by your health care provider. Use the heat source that your health
care provider recommends, such as a moist heat pack or a heating pad.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the heat source.
—46 Leave the heat on for 20–30 minutes.
—46 Remove the heat if your skin turns bright red. This is especially important if you are unable to feel pain, heat, or cold.
You have a greater risk of getting burned.
Activity
• Do not stay in bed. Staying in bed for more than 1–2 days can delay your recovery.
• Sit up and stand up straight. Avoid leaning forward when you sit or hunching over when you stand.
—46 If you work at a desk, sit close to it so you do not need to lean over. Keep your chin tucked in. Keep your neck drawn
back, and keep your elbows bent at a 90-degree angle (right angle).
—46 Sit high and close to the steering wheel when you drive. Add lower back (lumbar) support to your car seat, if needed.
• Take short walks on even surfaces as soon as you are able. Try to increase the length of time you walk each day.
• Do not sit, drive, or stand in one place for more than 30 minutes at a time. Sitting or standing for long periods of time can put
stress on your back.
• Do not drive or use heavy machinery while taking prescription pain medicine.
• Use proper lifting techniques. When you bend and lift, use positions that put less stress on your back:
—46 Bend your knees.

Emergency
—46 Keep the load close to your body.
—46 Avoid twisting.
• Exercise regularly as told by your health care provider. Exercising helps your back heal faster and helps prevent back injuries
by keeping muscles strong and flexible.
• Work with a physical therapist to make a safe exercise program, as recommended by your health care provider. Do any
exercises as told by your physical therapist.
Lifestyle
• Maintain a healthy weight. Extra weight puts stress on your back and makes it difficult to have good posture.
• Avoid activities or situations that make you feel anxious or stressed. Stress and anxiety increase muscle tension and can
make back pain worse. Learn ways to manage anxiety and stress, such as through exercise.
General instructions
• Sleep on a firm mattress in a comfortable position. Try lying on your side with your knees slightly bent. If you lie on your back,
put a pillow under your knees.
• Keep your head and neck in a straight line with your spine (neutral position) when using electronic equipment like
smartphones or pads. To do this:
—46 Raise your smartphone or pad to look at it instead of bending your head or neck to look down.
—46 Put the smartphone or pad at the level of your face while looking at the screen.
• Follow your treatment plan as told by your health care provider. This may include:
—46 Cognitive or behavioral therapy.
—46 Acupuncture or massage therapy.
—46 Meditation or yoga.
Contact a health care provider if:
• You have pain that is not relieved with rest or medicine.
• You have increasing pain going down into your legs or buttocks.
• Your pain does not improve after 2 weeks.
• You have pain at night.
• You lose weight without trying.
• You have a fever or chills.
• You develop nausea or vomiting.
• You develop abdominal pain.
Get help right away if:
• You develop new bowel or bladder control problems.
• You have unusual weakness or numbness in your arms or legs.
• You feel faint.
These symptoms may represent a serious problem that is an emergency. Do not wait to see if the symptoms will go away. Get
medical help right away. Call your local emergency services (911 in the U.S.). Do not drive yourself to the hospital.

Motor Vehicle Collision Injury, Adult
After a motor vehicle collision, it is common to have injuries to the head, face, arms, and body. These injuries may include cuts, burns,
and bruises. The collision can also cause sore muscles, muscle strains, headaches, and broken bones.
You may have stiffness and soreness for the first several hours. You may feel worse after waking up the first morning after the collision.
These injuries tend to feel worse for the first 24–48 hours. Your injuries should then begin to improve with each day. How quickly you
improve often depends on:
• The severity of the collision.
• The number of injuries you have.
• The location and nature of the injuries.
• Whether you were wearing a seat belt and whether your airbag deployed.
A head injury may result in a concussion, which is a brain injury that can have serious effects. If you have a concussion, you should rest
as told by your health care provider. You must be very careful to avoid having a second concussion.
Follow these instructions at home:
Medicines
• Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider.
• If you were prescribed antibiotics, take or apply it as told by your health care provider. Do not stop using the antibiotic even if
you start to feel better.
Wound or burn care
Follow instructions from your health care provider about how to take care of your wound or burn. Make sure you:

Take over-the-counter and prescription medicines only as told by your health care provider, and apply heat or ice as told.
This information is not intended to replace advice given to you by your health care provider. Make sure you discuss any questions you
have with your health care provider.

Emergency
• Clean your wound or burn. To do this:
—46 Wash it with mild soap and water.
—46 Rinse it with water to remove all soap.
—46 Pat it dry with a clean towel. Do not rub it.
—46 Put an ointment or cream on the wound, if you were told to do so.
• Know when and how to change or remove your bandage (dressing). Always wash your hands with soap and water for at least
20 seconds before and after you change your dressing. If soap and water are not available, use hand sanitizer.
• Leave any stitches (sutures), skin glue, or adhesive strips in place. These skin closures may need to stay in place for 2 weeks
or longer. If adhesive strip edges start to loosen and curl up, you may trim the loose edges. Do not remove adhesive strips
completely unless your health care provider tells you to do that.
• Avoid exposing your burn or wound to the sun.
• Keep the surface of the wound or burn intact.
—46 Do not scratch or pick at the wound or burn.
—46 Do not break any blisters you may have.
—46 Do not peel any skin.
• Check your wound or burn every day for signs of infection. Check for:
—46 Redness, swelling, or pain.
—46 Fluid or blood.
—46 Warmth.
—46 Pus or a bad smell.
Managing pain, stiffness, and swelling
• If directed, put ice on the injured areas. This can help with pain and swelling. To do this:
—46 Put ice in a plastic bag.
—46 Place a towel between your skin and the bag.
—46 Leave the ice on for 20 minutes, 2–3 times a day.
—46 If your skin turns bright red, remove the ice right away to prevent skin damage. The risk of skin damage is higher if
you cannot feel pain, heat, or cold.
—46 Raise (elevate) the wound or burn above the level of your heart while you are sitting or lying down. This will help
reduce pain, pressure, and swelling.
–52 If you have a wound or burn on your face, you may want to sleep with your head elevated. You may do this by putting
an extra pillow under your head.
Activity
• Rest. Rest helps your body to heal. Make sure you:
—46 Get plenty of sleep at night. Avoid staying up late.

—46 Keep the same bedtime hours on weekends and weekdays.

Emergency Awareness and Preventative Care
STROKE is an EMERGENCY
Every Minute Counts
Act FAST and Check for these signs:
FACE Does the face look uneven?
ARM Does one arm drift down?
SPEECH Does their speech sound
strange?
TIME Call 9-1-1 at any sign of stroke
Stroke Risk Factors
Atrial Fibrillation
(irregular heartbeat) Diabetes Family history ofstroke
Heart Disease Heavy alcohol use High Blood Pressure
High Cholesterol Physical inactivity
and obesity Smoking
Cigarette Smoking
The facts are clear, cigarette smoking will shorten your life. Smoking can cause many illnesses along the way. As a healthcare provider,
we recommend that you stop smoking. Assistance with quitting is available by contacting 1-800-QUIT-NOW. This is a free resource
providing counseling, support, and referral. Or you may contact your personal physician.
 
Don't Wait! Stop a Heart Attack Before It Starts
What is a heart attack?
A heart attack is damage or death to a part of the heart from severely decreased or lack of blood flow to the heart. Over time, arteries
can become narrow from the buildup of fat and cholesterol, which is called plaque. The plaque can rupture causing a blood clot to form.
When the blood clot forms, the artery can become severely narrowed or completely blocked, causing a heart attack.
• Heart attack is the leading cause of death in the United States.
• 85% of muscle damage occurs within the first 2 hours.
• Delay in the recognition of heart attack symptoms increases the chances of death.
Know the early symptoms of a heart attack:
Nausea
Feeling of
"fullness" in
chest
Jaw Pain
Pain that travels
down one or
both arms

There are unusual signs of heart attack, too!
Women, the elderly, and diabetics may present with atypical symptoms:
• Fainting/dizziness
• Weakness
• Confusion
Risk Factors for a Heart Attack
Some heart disease risk factors, such as age and family, cannot be changed. Others, like smoking and lack of exercise, can be
changed.
Smoking High Cholesterol Blood Pressure
Family History Obesity Age
Gender (Males are
at higher risk) Lack of Exercise Diabetes
Diet Stress Excessive Alcohol
Intake
If you or someone you know is experiencing the signs and symptoms of a heart attack, DON'T DELAY.
Call 9-1-1 immediately and seek help.
If someone collapses, perform CPR!
Do not attempt to drive if you are having symptoms of heart attack.
Why Hands-Only CPR?
• Hands-Only CPR has been shown to be as effective as conventional CPR for cardiac arrests that occur outside of a hospital.
• Survival depends on immediately receiving CPR from someone nearby.
How do you perform Hands-Only CPR?
There are two easy steps:
• 1. Call 9-1-1 if you see a teen or adult collapse
• 2. Push hard and fast in the center of the chest at a beat of 100 beats per minute
Save a life!
4 WAYS TO GET AHEAD OF SEPSIS
SEPSIS is a MEDICAL EMERGENCY. Time Matters!

Emergency
Infections put you and your family at risk for a life-threatening condition called sepsis.
• Sepsis is the body's extreme response to an infection. It is life-threatening, and without timely treatment, sepsis can rapidly lead
to tissue damage, organ failure, and death. Sepsis happens when an infection you already have-in your skin, lungs, urinary tract
or somewhere else-riggers a chain reaction throughout your body.
1 PREVENT
INFECTIONS
• Take good care of
chronic conditions.
• Talk to your doctor
about getting the
recommended
vaccines.
2 PRACTICE GOOD
HYGIENE
• Wash your hands
frequently.
• Keep cuts or open
sores clean and
covered until they
are healed.
3 KNOW THE
SYMPTOMS
• Confusion or
disorientation
• Shortness of breath
• High heart rate
• Fever, shivering, or
feeling very cold
• Extreme pain or
discomfort
• Clammy or sweaty
skin
4 ACT FAST
• Get medical care
IMMEDIATELY if
you suspect sepsis
or if you have an
infection that is not
getting better or is
getting worse.
To learn more about sepsis and how to prevent infections, visit www.cdc.gov/sepsis.

Emergency
Behavioral / Mental Health Resources at UofL Health
If you or a loved one needs mental health, suicide, or substance use related crisis support, call or text 988
(1-[PHONE-319]) - National Suicide & Crisis Lifeline to connect with a trained crisis counselor. If this is a medical
emergency, dial 911. Walk-In assessments are welcome at all UofL Health Emergency Departments and UofL Health -
Peace Hospital.
UofL Health – UofL Hospital Emergency Psychiatric Services For questions or concerns, call [PHONE-318].
Adults, may be:
• Discharged with an outpatient resource that is appropriate to their needs.
• Admitted to EPS’s Holding Bed Unit for observation or transferred to another hospital via ambulance.
• A team of psychiatrists, psychiatric nurse practitioners and social workers determine the best treatment options.
UofL Health – Mary & Elizabeth Hospital 
Adult Inpatient Medical Detoxification from alcohol, opioids, benzodiazepines, and various other addictive
substances in a safe and monitored environment.
• Support groups, Group therapy, Certified peer support specialists.
• After care services and connecting patients with community resources.
• Alcoholic Anonymous (AA) meeting available onsite.
For Adult Inpatient Medical Detoxification admission or services call [PHONE-317].
Adult Medical Behavioral Health Unit can provide treatment and care for medically compromised patients.
Behavioral health services include:
• Acute crisis stabilization, treatment of acute psychiatric symptoms
• Group/individual therapy
• Behavior and medical management
For Adult Medical Behavioral Health Unit services or information about admission, please call [PHONE-316]. 
UofL Health – Peace Hospital Open 24/7 at 2020 Newburg Rd., Louisville, KY 40205 – [PHONE-315]). 
 
Treatment for psychiatric and substance use disorders.

The examination and treatment you have received in the Emergency Department has been done to provide an appropriate evaluation
and stabilizing treatment on an emergency basis only. Given the limited resources, it is not meant to be a substitute for complete
medical care. The follow-up provider you named will receive a copy of your records and all test reports. IT IS IMPORTANT THAT YOU
SCHEDULE A FOLLOW-UP APPOINTMENT AND BE RE-EVALUATED. You should report any new complaints, symptoms, or
remaining problems at that time. IT IS IMPOSSIBLE FOR THE EMERGENCY DEPARTMENT TO RECOGNIZE AND TREAT ALL
ELEMENTS OF INJURY OR ILLNESS IN A SINGLE VISIT.
If you have been referred to a specialist provider, it means that we believe you may have a condition that requires the expertise of a
specialist. These providers work in partnership with the hospital and have agreed to see referred patients in their office for further
evaluation. KEEP IN MIND THAT THE SPECIALIST HAS HIS/HER OWN OFFICE POLICIES WHICH MAY REQUIRE PROPER
INSURANCE OR PAYMENT UP FRONT BEFORE THE SPECIALIST WILL SEE YOU. It is your responsibility to call the specialist
provider to make an appointment. We do not have the ability to refer patients to specialists/physicians that work with specific insurance
companies.
Please be advised that all financial charges or billing practices are determined by that practice, not the hospital. If your insurance
company requires that you see a specialist from their approved list, it is your responsibility to contact your insurance company to make
those arrangements. It is also your responsibility to follow any other requirements of your insurance company necessary to obtain
coverage for claims submitted.
I hereby acknowledge receipt of these instructions and information above. I understand that I have received Emergency Treatment only,
which is not a substitute for complete medical care and acknowledge that all of my medical problems may not be known, identified, or
treated prior to my release. I understand the need to arrange follow-up care with the provider as indicated. I understand that I should
contact my primary care provider immediately or return to the Emergency Department, if my condition worsens, fails to improve, or new
symptoms appear.

Reason For Exam
(CT Spine Lumbar Recon WO) RM 9, MVA
Report
CT Spine Thoracic Recon WO, CT Spine Lumbar Recon WO
ACCESSION NUMBER: 40CT250050542, 40CT250050543
DATE: 9/3/2025 16:12
PROVIDED INDICATION: RM 9, MVA
COMPARISON: None.
STUDY QUALITY: Adequate
TECHNIQUE: Reconstructed CT THORACIC AND LUMBAR spine images with reformatted sagittal and coronal images.
All CT exams at this location are performed using dose modulation techniques as appropriate to a performed exam
including the following: automated exposure control; adjustment of the mA and/or kV according to patient size (this
includes techniques or standardized protocols for targeted exams where dose is matched to indication/reason for exam;
i.e. extremities or head); use of iterative reconstruction techniques.
FINDINGS:
THORACIC SPINE: Thoracic alignment is relatively anatomic. Disc spaces are relatively preserved. 8 x 6 mm sclerotic
focus in the posterior body of T3, could potentially represent a bone island. If there is a history of, or concern for neoplasia
recommend bone scan for further evaluation. No acute fracture, subluxation or dislocation identified at this time. No
perivertebral soft tissue swelling.
LUMBAR SPINE: Lumbar alignment is relatively anatomic. Disc spaces are relatively preserved. Early, incomplete, or
partial sacralization of L5 on the left. L5-S1 pseudarthrosis on the left. No acute fracture, subluxation or dislocation
identified at this time. No perivertebral soft tissue swelling.
IMPRESSION:
1. No acute thoracic or lumbar spine fracture. Recommend dermatome mapping for further evaluation.
2. 8 x 6 mm sclerotic focus in the posterior body of T3, could potentially represent a bone island. If there is a history of, or
concern for neoplasia recommend bone scan for further evaluation.

modulation techniques as appropriate to a performed exam including the following: automated exposure control;
adjustment of the mA and/or kV according to patient size (this includes techniques or standardized protocols for targeted
exams where dose is matched to indication/reason for exam; i.e. extremities or head); use of iterative reconstruction
techniques.
FINDINGS:
Parenchyma: No acute intracranial hemorrhage, mass effect, midline shift, intra or extra-axial fluid collection present.
Gray-white differentiation appears maintained.
Ventricles: The ventricles, sulci, and cisterns are age-appropriate.
Soft tissues: Negative
Bones: No acute calvarial fracture seen.
Visualized paranasal sinuses: Scattered sinus disease. Retention cysts versus polyps in the maxillary and sphenoid
sinuses. Near complete opacification of the right frontal sinus.
Mastoid air cells: Appropriately pneumatized.
External auditory canals: Soft tissue within the external auditory canals bilaterally. This is worse on the left. Likely
cerumen. Recommend direct visualization for confirmation.
IMPRESSION:
1. No acute intracranial hemorrhage or calvarial fracture identified.
2. Sinus disease.
3. Soft tissue in the external auditory canals. Recommend direct visualization to confirm potential cerumen.

Coagulation
Collected Date
Collected Time
9/3/2025
15:50 EDT
Procedure Units Ref Range
PT 10.6 #1 Second(s) [9.7-11.5]
INR 1.0 #2
PTT 27.3 #3 Second(s) [23.3-33.2]
Interpretive Data
#1: PT
When using the PT to screen for a coagulopathy, please refer to the PT reference
range to evaluate results.
#2: INR
To monitor warfarin, the INR calculated from the PT is used, according to current
published guidelines:
*Most indications, moderate intensity INR (2.0-3.0) is effective.
*Patients with recurrent thromboembolic events with a therapeutic INR as above, or
other additional risk factors for thromboembolic events, high intensity INR
(2.5-3.5) is recommended.
*Optimal target range for the INR is not likely to be the same for all indications,
and lower INR targets may be prudent for patients at very high risk of bleeding.
The INR is used to manage patients on warfarin, and thus is not compared to a
"normal" INR range. The validity of the INR in other conditions of impaired
coagulation has not been fully evaluated, and the PT recorded in seconds is
recommended in these instances. Ref: CHEST June 2008 supplement.
#3: PTT
 
To screen for coagulaopathy, refer to reference range in seconds.
 
To monitor intravenous unfractionated heparin, the therapeutic aPTT range has been
determined by this laboratory to be 42.5 - 57.3 seconds. Patients who require high
doses of heparin to achieve a therapeutic aPTT, or in patients with a prolonged
baseline aPTT (i.e. lupus anticoagulant), it is reasonable to adjust heparin doses
based on anti Xa levels (unfractionated heparin assay to acheive a level of 0.3 -
0.7 IU/mL. The aPTT is also used to monitor direct thrombin inhibitors as per
pharmacy protocols.

Authorization and Notice of Privacy Practices ("NPP"): my permission is required by law, by signing this form I
agree that UofL Health may receive, use and disclose my Health Information as set forth in this Consent and as set
forth in UofL Health's NPP. I understand that I can find more information about my rights to my Health Information,
and about how UofL Health uses my Health Information, in the NPP. I acknowledge that if I requested a copy of the
NPP that I have been given a copy. I further understand that the NPP is available on UofL Health's website at:
www.uoflhealth.org.
I agree that my permission applies to all of my Health Information in UofL Health's possession, including but not
limited to my contact information, problem list, diagnostic test results, medication list, allergy list, immunizations,
medical history, surgeries, procedures, and other clinically relevant data.
I understand that UofL Health cannot control how others that receive my Health Information will protect or use my
information. I understand that others may not be required by law to protect my Health Information.
I understand that UofL Health is a research and teaching institution and my data and body parts, including organs,
tissue, bone, or bodily fluids removed for diagnostic and/or therapeutic purposes may be used for teaching and
research purposes. My data and body parts will be treated carefully so that I cannot be identified, except as required
or permitted by law. I agree that I do not own my body parts after removal and I have no rights to the research
products from these parts.
Purposes for which my Health Information may be shared: I understand that UofL Health may receive, use, and
disclose my Health Information for the purposes outlined in the NPP. In particular, UofL Health may use and disclose
my Health Information for the following purposes:
Data Sharing Program Purposes: I understand and agree that the use and disclosure of my health information for
certain aspects of treatment at UofL Health may be disclosed to other people involved with my care outside UofL
Health. If I desire to revoke my consent, even in an emergency situation, I must notify UofL Health's Health
Information Management Department by phone: [PHONE-435], option 2. I understand and agree that my request
will be evaluated to determine if it is reasonable and in the best interest of my health care to comply with my request.
I will be notified in writing of as to whether UofL Health will be able to grant my request. If my request is granted and I
am are in need of emergency treatment, UofL Health may end the restriction if the information is needed to provide
my care. (See our Notice of Privacy Practices for more information on these types of uses and disclosures for
further information.)
Fundraising Activities: UofL Health relies on fundraising to help support caring for all patients. I give my permission
to be contacted relating to fundraising opportunities. If I prefer not to be contacted about fundraising, I must notify
UofL Health by email to: [EMAIL-436] or by phone [PHONE-437]
Operational Purposes: I agree that the contact information I give to UofL Health, such as telephone numbers and
email addresses, may be used by UofL Health and third parties acting for UofL Health to communicate with me for
operational purposes including appointment reminders, follow up treatment reminders, flu shot reminders, and
patient surveys.
Marketing Purposes: I further agree that the contact information I give to UofL Health may be used by UofL Health
and third parties acting for UofL Health to communicate with me for commercial, advertising or marketing activities,
including collection or billing matters. I understand and expressly consent to be contacted by auto-dialed and/or
artificial or pre-recorded text messages or telephone calls or voicemails at the number I provided to UofL Health. I
understand that my consent is not required as a condition of purchasing or receiving any goods or services from
UofL Health. If I desire to revoke my consent, or do not want to be contacted for marketing purposes, I must notify
UofL Health by calling [PHONE-438] or by email: [EMAIL-439]

an auto dialer or other computer assisted technology, pre-recorded message(s), or by any other form of electronic
communication for any purpose including, but not limited to, appointment and follow-up health care reminders,
scheduling, my account(s), assignment of benefits, and/or financial responsibility. I understand that depending on my
phone plan I could be charged for these calls or text messages. I agree to provide new number(s) if my number(s)
change(s). Providing these numbers is not a condition of receiving healthcare services.
USING AND SHARING MY INFORMATION
The Law: There is a federal law called the Health Insurance Portability and Accountability Act of 1996 ("HIPAA").
This law requires UofL Health to protect the privacy and security of its patients' treatment, contact, and financial
information. Taken together, this information is called your "Health Information". There are also other federal and/or
state laws that require UofL Health to take additional steps to protect certain categories of Health Information,
including, but not limited to, Health Information about behavioral or mental health; developmental disabilities;
treatment for substance abuse (alcohol and/or drugs) disorders; genetic testing and counseling; HIV/AIDS; sexual
assault/ abuse; sexually transmitted illnesses; pregnancy; birth control; domestic abuse of an adult with a disability;
child abuse and neglect.

General Consent on Admission
The term "UofL Health" means UofL Health at any of its hospitals, offices, and/or other locations as well as all of
University of Louisville Physicians, nurses, and other staff, employees or affiliates.
I give my consent to UofL Health providing care and treatment, including consultation, during the course of my
admission to UofL Health. By signing this consent form, I consent to each of the following:
TREATMENT and RECOGNITION OF INDEPENDENT CONTRACTORS
I have a condition requiring examination, diagnosis and treatment. I consent to and authorize such care including but
not limited to: X-ray, laboratory, routine diagnostic tests and therapeutic procedures ("Services") performed by my
admitting and treating physicians.
I understand and acknowledge that Physicians and certain other practitioners who may treat me or have involvement
in my care are not employees of UofL Health or any of its facilities. I also understand that UofL Health and its
facilities are not responsible for the actions of physicians and other independent contractor practitioners who treat me
or have involvement in my care at the UofL Health facilities. I further understand these independent contractors
include Physicians, groups of physicians or other practitioners, including, but not limited to, nurses employed by
physician groups, certified registered nurse anesthetists (CRNAs), and Physicians' assistants employed by physician
groups. I understand that the physicians include, but are not limited to, emergency room physicians, radiologists,
anesthesiologists, surgeons, internists, etc. I also understand that there may be medical students, medical and
surgical residents in various fields, and/or fellows involved in my care and that these individuals are not employed or
otherwise agents of the UofL Health or its facilities. I further understand that UofL Heath and its facilities are not
liable for their actions. I understand that at times, the facility may bill for physician services under a contractual
agreement and that UofL Health does not assume liability for the independent contractors' actions by providing this
service.
I understand that my treatment may involve risks and that there are no guarantees concerning the outcome or results
of this treatment and/or examination and I have the right to make decisions concerning my health care, including the
right to refuse medical and surgical procedures/treatment.
I understand that UofL Health uses artificial intelligence technology for clinical treatment purposes. The purpose of
using artificial intelligence is to assist in my diagnosis and treatment. Use of artificial intelligence does not replace a
clinician's clinical judgement and is only used to enhance the care I receive.
TESTING FOR INFECTIOUS DISEASES
I understand that as part of my medical treatment, procedures or testing, I may be tested for Human
Immunodeficiency Virus ("HIV"), Hepatitis, or any other blood borne infectious disease as well COVID-19 or any
airborne pathogen if a physician or advanced practice registered nurse orders the test for diagnostic purposes. I also
understand that, in the case of exposure of a health care provider or first responder (such as an emergency worker,
fire fighter or police officer) to my bodily fluids, although I will be informed of the right to consent to testing for HIV or
other infectious diseases transmitted by bodily fluids, in most cases, tests may be performed on previously gathered
bodily fluid samples or a court order may be obtained to compel such testing. Information concerning the fact that a
test was ordered and the results of such test will remain confidential and be disclosed by UofL Health only as
permitted by law.
AUTHORIZATION OF REPRESENTATIVE TO APPEAL
I understand that Medicare and other payers do not pay the difference in the cost between a private and
semi-private room when use of a private room is not necessary for medical reasons. I hereby agree that the
difference in the cost between a semi-private and private room will be my responsibility to pay if I request one at any
point during my stay.
I hereby authorize and convey to UofL Health the full extent permissible under Federal and State law and under any
applicable insurance policy and/or employee health care benefit plan: (1) the right and ability to act as my Authorized
Representative in connection with any claim, right, matter, or cause of action that I may have under such insurance
policy and/or benefit plan; and (2) the right and ability to act as my Authorized Representative to pursue such claim,
right, matter, or cause of action in connection with said insurance policy and/or benefit plan, including the right and
ability to act as my Authorized Representative with respect to a benefit plan governed by the provisions of the
Employee Retirement Income Security Act ("ERISA").
